RAW ORDERS (`/app/raw_orders/`)\n\n**File Naming Pattern:** `day_XXX_S_Y_[format-type].[extension]`\n- `XXX` = day number (001-365)\n- `Y` = store number (1-10)\n- Format type varies per file\n\n**Data Span:** 365 days, 10 stores (S_1 through S_10)\n\n**Format Types (4 different formats per day per store):**\n\n#### Format 1: Text Template (`text-template.txt`)\nEach line contains a natural language order statement.\n\n**Schema:**\n```\n[line_number]<TAB>Order from Day_[day]. Please deliver [qty] units of product [product_id]. Regards, Store [store_id].\n```\n\n**Example:** `/app/raw_orders/day_001_S_1_text-template.txt`\n```\n1\tOrder from Day_1. Please deliver 81 units of product P_1. Regards, Store S_1.\n2\tOrder from Day_1. Please deliver 67 units of product P_2. Regards, Store S_1.\n...\n```\n\n#### Format 2: Key-Value (`key-value.txt`)\nPipe-separated key-value pairs with structured order information.\n\n**Schema:**\n```\n[line_number]<TAB>RECEIVER: [store_id] | ORDER_PRODUCT: [product_id] | ORDER_QTY: [qty]\n```\n\n**Example:** `/app/raw_orders/day_001_S_2_key-value.txt`\n```\n1\tRECEIVER: S_2 | ORDER_PRODUCT: P_1 | ORDER_QTY: 55\n2\tRECEIVER: S_2 | ORDER_PRODUCT: P_2 | ORDER_QTY: 43\n...\n```\n\n#### Format 3: Table CSV (`table-csv.csv`)\nSemicolon-separated values with product and quantity.\n\n**Schema:**\n```\nPRODUCT;QUANTITY\n[product_id];[qty]\n```\n\n**Example:** `/app/raw_orders/day_001_S_3_table-csv.csv`\n```\nPRODUCT;QUANTITY\nP_1;58\nP_2;51\nP_3;54\n...\n```\n\n#### Format 4: API JSON (`api-json.json`)\nStructured JSON format with nested items array.\n\n**Schema:**\n```json\n{\n  \"store_id\": \"[store_id]\",\n  \"date\": \"Day_[day]\",\n  \"items\": [\n    {\n      \"prod_id\": \"[product_id]\",\n      \"qty\": [qty]\n    },\n    ...\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n**Example:** `/app/raw_orders/day_001_S_10_api-json.json`\n```json\n{\n  \"store_id\": \"S_10\",\n  \"date\": \"Day_1\",\n  \"items\": [\n    {\"prod_id\": \"P_1\", \"qty\": 69},\n    {\"prod_id\": \"P_2\", \"qty\": 81},\n    ...\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 2. information.\n\n**Schema:**\n```\n[line_number]<TAB>SUPPLIER: PR_[supplier_id] | DAY: [day]\n[line_number]<TAB>PRODUCT: [product_id] | DELIVERED_QTY: [qty]\n```\n\n**Example:** `/app/raw_supplier_receipts/day_001_PR_11_key-value.txt`\n```\n1\tSUPPLIER: PR_11 | DAY: 1\n2\tPRODUCT: P_1 | DELIVERED_QTY: 14\n3\tPRODUCT: P_2 | DELIVERED_QTY: 12\n...\n```\n\n#### Format 3: Table CSV (`table-csv.csv`)\nSemicolon-separated values with product and delivered quantity.\n\n**Schema:**\n```\nPRODUCT;DELIVERED_QTY\n[product_id];[qty]\n```\n\n**Example:** `/app/raw_supplier_receipts/day_001_PR_13_table-csv.csv`\n```\nPRODUCT;DELIVERED_QTY\nP_5;11\nP_8;11\nP_9;13\n...\n```\n\n#### Format 4: API JSON (`api-json.json`)\nStructured JSON format with nested Regards, Store S_1.\n...\n```\n\n#### Format 2: Key-Value (`key-value.txt`)\nPipe-separated key-value pairs with structured order information.\n\n**Schema:**\n```\n[line_number]<TAB>RECEIVER: [store_id] | ORDER_PRODUCT: [product_id] | ORDER_QTY: [qty]\n```\n\n**Example:** `/app/raw_orders/day_001_S_2_key-value.txt`\n```\n1\tRECEIVER: S_2 | ORDER_PRODUCT: P_1 | ORDER_QTY: 55\n2\tRECEIVER: S_2 | ORDER_PRODUCT: P_2 | ORDER_QTY: 43\n...\n```\n\n#### Format 3: Table CSV (`table-csv.csv`)\nSemicolon-separated values with product and quantity.\n\n**Schema:**\n```\nPRODUCT;QUANTITY\n[product_id];[qty]\n```\n\n**Example:** `/app/raw_orders/day_001_S_3_table-csv.csv`\n```\nPRODUCT;QUANTITY\nP_1;58\nP_2;51\nP_3;54\n...\n```\n\n#### Format 4: API JSON (`api-json.json`)\nStructured JSON format with nested items array.\n\n**Schema:**\n```json\n{\n  \"store_id\": \"[store_id]\",\n  \"date\": \"Day_[day]\",\n  \"items\": [\n    {\n      \"prod_id\": \"[product_id]\",\n      \"qty\": [qty]\n    },\n    ...\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n**Example:** `/app/raw_orders/day_001_S_10_api-json.json`\n```json\n{\n  \"store_id\": \"S_10\",\n  \"date\": \"Day_1\",\n  \"items\": [\n    {\"prod_id\": \"P_1\", \"qty\": 69},\n    {\"prod_id\": \"P_2\", \"qty\": 81},\n    ...\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 2. RAW SUPPLIER RECEIPTS (`/app/raw_supplier_receipts/`)\n\n**File Naming Pattern:** `day_XXX_PR_YY_[format-type].[extension]`\n- `XXX` = day number (001-365)\n- `YY` = supplier/provider number (01-60, named PR_1 to PR_60)\n- Format type varies per file\n\n**Data Span:** 365 days, 60 suppliers (PR_1 through PR_60)\n\n**Format Types (4 different formats per day per supplier):**\n\n#### Format 1: Text Template (`text-template.txt`)\nNatural language delivery statements.\n\n**Schema:**\n```\n[line_number]<TAB>Supplier PR_[supplier_id] delivered [qty] units of product [product_id] to the wholesaler on Day_[day].\n```\n\n**Example:** `/app/raw_supplier_receipts/day_001_PR_10_text-template.txt`\n```\n1\tSupplier PR_10 delivered 12 units of product P_1 to the wholesaler on Day_1.\n2\tSupplier PR_10 delivered 10 units of product P_2 to the wholesaler on Day_1.\n...\n```\n\n#### Format 2: Key-Value (`key-value.txt`)\nPipe-separated key-value pairs with supplier and product information.\n\n**Schema:**\n```\n[line_number]<TAB>SUPPLIER: PR_[supplier_id] | DAY: [day]\n[line_number]<TAB>PRODUCT: [product_id] | DELIVERED_QTY: [qty]\n```\n\n**Example:** `/app/raw_supplier_receipts/day_001_PR_11_key-value.txt`\n```\n1\tSUPPLIER: PR_11 | DAY: 1\n2\tPRODUCT: P_1 | DELIVERED_QTY: 14\n3\tPRODUCT: P_2 | DELIVERED_QTY: 12\n...\n```\n\n#### Format 3: Table CSV (`table-csv.csv`)\nSemicolon-separated values with product and delivered quantity.\n\n**Schema:**\n```\nPRODUCT;DELIVERED_QTY\n[product_id];[qty]\n```\n\n**Example:** `/app/raw_supplier_receipts/day_001_PR_13_table-csv.csv`\n```\nPRODUCT;DELIVERED_QTY\nP_5;11\nP_8;11\nP_9;13\n...\n```\n\n#### Format 4: API JSON (`api-json.json`)\nStructured JSON format with nested items array.\n\n**Schema:**\n```json\n{\n  \"supplier_id\": \"PR_[supplier_id]\",\n  \"date\": \"Day_[day]\",\n  \"items\": [\n    {\n      \"prod_id\": \"[product_id]\",\n      \"delivered_qty\": [qty]\n    },\n    ...\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n**Example:** `/app/raw_supplier_receipts/day_001_PR_12_api-json.json`\n```json\n{\n  \"supplier_id\": \"PR_12\",\n  \"date\": \"Day_1\",\n  \"items\": [\n    {\"prod_id\": \"P_6\", \"delivered_qty\": 12},\n    {\"prod_id\": \"P_8\", \"delivered_qty\": 11},\n    ...\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 3. RAW WHOLESALER RECEIPTS (`/app/raw_wholesaler_receipts/`)\n\n**File Naming Pattern:** `day_XXX_PR_YY_receipt.txt`\n- `XXX` = day number (001-365)\n- `YY` = supplier/provider number (01-60)\n- All files are simple text receipts\n\n**Data Span:** 365 days, 60 suppliers\n\n**Format:** Simplified key-value format with minimal information\n\n**Schema:**\n```\nDAY: [day_number]\nSUPPLIER_ID: PR_[supplier_id]\nDAILY_SEQUENCE_NO: [sequence_number]\n```\n\n**Example:** `/app/raw_wholesaler_receipts/day_001_PR_10_receipt.txt`\n```\nDAY: 1\nSUPPLIER_ID: PR_10\nDAILY_SEQUENCE_NO: 55\n```\n\n**Note:** These are lightweight receipts that appear to be confirmation/acknowledgment records with a sequence number tracking deliveries.\n\n---\n\n### 4. RAW WHOLESALER STORE RECEIPTS (`/app/raw_wholesaler_store_receipts/`)\n\n**File Naming Pattern:** `day_XXX_S_Y_receipt.txt`\n- `XXX` = day number (001-365)\n- `Y` = store number (1-10)\n- All files are simple text receipts\n\n**Data Span:** 365 days, 10 stores\n\n**Format:** Key-value format with total delivery information\n\n**Schema:**\n```\nDAY: [day_number]\nSTORE_ID: S_[store_id]\nDAILY_SEQUENCE_NO: [sequence_number]\nTOTAL_DELIVERED_UNITS: [total_units]\n```\n\n**Examples:**\n- `/app/raw_wholesaler_store_receipts/day_001_S_1_receipt.txt`\n  ```\n  DAY: 1\n  STORE_ID: S_1\n  DAILY_SEQUENCE_NO: 1\n  TOTAL_DELIVERED_UNITS: 2539\n  ```\n\n- `/app/raw_wholesaler_store_receipts/day_001_S_5_receipt.txt`\n  ```\n  DAY: 1\n  STORE_ID: S_5\n  DAILY_SEQUENCE_NO: 5\n  TOTAL_DELIVERED_UNITS: 1258\n  ```\n\n**Note:** These track the aggregate quantities delivered to each store per day with daily sequence numbering.\n\n---\n\n### 5. SALES LOG (`/app/sales_log.csv`)\n\n**File Location:** `/app/sales_log.csv`\n\n**File Size:** 53.5 MB\n\n**Format:** Comma-separated values with headers\n\n**Schema:**\n```\nDay,Store_ID,Product_ID,Reported_Demand,Sold_Quantity,Lost_Sales\n[day_number],[store_id],[product_id],[demand_qty],[sold_qty],[lost_sales_qty]\n```\n\n**Columns:**\n- `Day`: Integer day number (1+)\n- `Store_ID`: Store identifier (S_1 to S_10)\n- `Product_ID`: Product identifier (P_1 to P_30)\n- `Reported_Demand`: Quantity demanded by the store\n- `Sold_Quantity`: Quantity actually sold\n- `Lost_Sales`: Quantity of unmet demand (Reported_Demand - Sold_Quantity)\n\n**Example from first 100 lines:** `/app/sales_log.csv`\n```\nDay,Store_ID,Product_ID,Reported_Demand,Sold_Quantity,Lost_Sales\n1,S_1,P_1,3,0,3\n1,S_1,P_2,3,0,3\n1,S_1,P_3,2,0,2\n1,S_1,P_4,2,0,2\n...\n```\n\n**Note:** In the sampled data, all Sold_Quantity values are 0 with lost sales equal to reported demand, suggesting inventory was not available on day 1.\n\n---\n\n### Key Patterns\n\n1. **Multiple Format Encoding:** The raw order and supplier receipt data are deliberately stored in 4 different formats (text, key-value, CSV, JSON) for the same logical information—likely a test scenario for handling heterogeneous data sources.\n\n2. **Entity Coverage:**\n   - Fulfill stores in sequence order (brutal first-come)\n        if day not in store_orders or day not in store_seq:\n            continue\n\n        sorted_stores = sorted(store_seq[day].keys(), key=lambda s: store_seq[day][s])\n\n        for store in sorted_stores:\n            if store not in store_orders[day]:\n                continue\n            for prod, ordered_qty in store_orders[day][store].items():\n                remaining = ordered_qty\n                alloc = {}\n                while remaining > 0 and wh_fifo[prod]:\n                    front = wh_fifo[prod][0]\n                    supp, avail = front\n                    take = min(remaining, avail)\n                    alloc[supp] = alloc.get(supp, 0) + take\n                    remaining -= take\n                    if avail <= take:\n                        wh_fifo[prod].popleft()\n                    else:\n                        wh_fifo[prod][0][1] = avail - take\n                if alloc:\n                    store_received[(day, store, prod)] = alloc\n\n    return store_received\n\n\n# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n# 3. BUILD STORE FIFO INVENTORY\n# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\ndef build_store_inventory_and_track(store_received, agg_sold, all_days, all_stores, all_products):\n    \"\"\"\n    Simulate store FIFO inventory and track which supplier's batches\n    are consumed on each (day, store, product).\n\n    Returns:\n        consumed_by: {(day, store, product): {supplier: qty_consumed}}\n    \"\"\"\n    # store_inv[store][product] = deque of [supplier, qty]\n    store_inv = defaultdict(lambda: defaultdict(deque))\n    consumed_by = {}\n\n    for day in all_days:\n        # Receive deliveries from wholesaler\n        for store in all_stores:\n            for prod in all_products:\n                delivery = store_received.get((day, store, prod), {})\n                for supp, qty in delivery.items():\n                    store_inv[store][prod].append([supp, qty])\n\n        # Consume based on sold quantity\n        for store in all_stores:\n            for prod in all_products:\n                sold = agg_sold.get((day, store, prod), 0)\n                if sold == 0:\n                    continue\n                remaining = sold\n                consumed = {}\n                inv = store_inv[store][prod]\n                while remaining > 0 and inv:\n                    front = inv[0]\n                    supp, avail = front\n                    take = min(remaining, avail)\n                    consumed[supp] = consumed.get(supp, 0) + take\n                    remaining -= take\n                    if avail <= take:\n                        inv.popleft()\n                    else:\n                        inv[0][1] = avail - take\n                if consumed:\n                    consumed_by[(day, store, prod)] = consumed\n\n    return consumed_by\n\n\n# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n# 4. DETECT QUALITY REJECTIONS\n# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\ndef detect_quality_rejections(agg_demand, all_days, all_stores, all_products):\n    \"\"\"\n    Detect demand drops matching the quality recovery pattern.\n\n    Quality recovery pattern (after rejection day X):\n      Days X+1..X+3:  ~20% of baseline\n      Days X+4..X+7:  ~50% of baseline\n      Days X+8..X+14: ~80% of baseline\n\n    Strategy:\n    1. For each product, compute cross-store calendar signal (average demand/day).\n    2. For each (store, product), compute normalized demand = demand / cross_avg.\n    3. Compute the store's own median normalized ratio as a size factor.\n    4. Deviation = normalized / size_factor.\n    5. Look for windows matching the recovery pattern shape.\n\n    Returns:\n        rejections: list of (store, product, rejection_day)\n            where rejection_day is the last \"normal\" day before the drop.\n    \"\"\"\n    # Cross-store average demand per (day, product) = calendar signal\n    cross_avg = defaultdict(float)\n    cross_cnt = defaultdict(int)\n    for (day, store, prod), d in agg_demand.items():\n        cross_avg[(day, prod)] += d\n        cross_cnt[(day, prod)] += 1\n    for k in cross_avg:\n        cross_avg[k] /= cross_cnt[k]\n\n    # Per (store, product), normalized trajectory\n    sp_norm = defaultdict(dict)\n    for (day, store, prod), d in agg_demand.items():\n        avg = cross_avg.get((day, prod), 0)\n        if avg > 5:\n            sp_norm[(store, prod)][day] = d / avg\n\n    rejections = []\n\n    for (store, prod), day_norm in sp_norm.items():\n        days_sorted = sorted(day_norm.keys())\n        if len(days_sorted) < 30:\n            continue\n\n        vals = [day_norm[d] for d in days_sorted]\n        # Store size factor: robust estimate of its relative size\n        size_factor = statistics.median(vals)\n        if size_factor < 0.05:\n            continue\n\n        # Day-indexed dict\n        dn = day_norm\n\n        for i, day in enumerate(days_sorted):\n            # Need at least 15 days ahead\n            if day > max(all_days) - 15:\n                continue\n\n            # Current deviation (normalized ratio / size_factor)\n            curr = dn.get(day, size_factor) / size_factor\n\n            # Look at next 14 days\n            future_devs = []\n            for offset in range(1, 15):\n                fd = day + offset\n                future_devs.append(dn.get(fd, size_factor) / size_factor)\n\n            if len(future_devs) < 14:\n                continue\n\n            # Previous 7 days (excluding current)\n            prev_devs = [dn.get(day - j, size_factor) / size_factor\n                         for j in range(1, 8) if (day - j) in dn]\n            if len(prev_devs) < 3:\n                continue\n            prev_avg = statistics.mean(prev_devs)\n\n            # Skip if recent history is already depressed (ongoing recovery)\n            if prev_avg < 0.75:\n                continue\n\n            # Current day should still be near normal\n            if curr < 0.70:\n                continue\n\n            # future_devs[0..2]  = recovery days 1-3  (should be ~20%)\n            # future_devs[3..6]  = recovery days 4-7  (should be ~50%)\n            # future_devs[7..13] = recovery days 8-14 (should be ~80%)\n            phase1 = statistics.mean(future_devs[0:3])\n            phase2 = statistics.mean(future_devs[3:7])\n            phase3 = statistics.mean(future_devs[7:14])\n\n            # Conditions for quality rejection pattern:\n            # phase1 significantly below normal\n            # phase2 > phase1\n            # phase3 > phase2\n            # All phases below the pre-rejection level\n            if (phase1 < 0.55 and\n                phase2 > phase1 * 1.2 and\n                phase3 > phase2 * 1.1 and\n                phase3 < 0.98 and\n                phase2 < 0.85):\n                rejections.append({\n                    'store': store,\n                    'product': prod,\n                    'rejection_day': day,\n                    'phase1': phase1,\n                    'phase2': phase2,\n                    'phase3': phase3,\n                    'prev_avg': prev_avg,\n                })\n\n    return rejections\n\n\n# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n# 5. ATTRIBUTE TO SUPPLIERS\n# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\ndef attribute_rejections(rejections, consumed_by, store_received):\n    \"\"\"\n    For each detected rejection, find the responsible supplier.\n\n    The rejection affects consumers who bought from the bad batch\n    on or just before the rejection_day. So we check which supplier's\n    units were being consumed on rejection_day and the few days before.\n\n    For \"confirmed\" status, we need clear attribution:\n    - The supplier was the sole or dominant source for the store at that time.\n    \"\"\"\n    confirmed = defaultdict(set)\n\n    for rej in rejections:\n        store = rej['store']\n        prod = rej['product']\n        rday = rej['rejection_day']\n\n        # The bad batch was consumed around rday.\n        # Check consumed_by for rday and a window before (batch might span days).\n        candidate_suppliers = defaultdict(int)\n        for check_day in range(max(1, rday - 5), rday + 2):\n            consumed = consumed_by.get((check_day, store, prod), {})\n            for supp, qty in consumed.items():\n                candidate_suppliers[supp] += qty\n\n        if not candidate_suppliers:\n            continue\n\n        total_qty = sum(candidate_suppliers.values())\n        if total_qty == 0:\n            continue\n\n        # Find dominant supplier(s)\n        max_qty = max(candidate_suppliers.values())\n        dominant = [s for s, q in candidate_suppliers.items()\n                    if q >= 0.6 * max_qty and q / total_qty > 0.3]\n\n        # For \"confirmed\" – require strong dominance:\n        # Either sole supplier, or one supplier with >70% of consumed units\n        sole = [s for s, q in candidate_suppliers.items()\n                if q / total_qty > 0.70]\n\n        if sole:\n            for s in sole:\n                confirmed[prod].add(s)\n        elif len(candidate_suppliers) == 1:\n            s = list(candidate_suppliers.keys())[0]\n            confirmed[prod].add(s)\n\n    return confirmed\n\n\n# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n# MAIN\n# {len(rejections)} potential quality rejection events found\")\n\n    # Print top rejections for debugging\n    rejections.sort(key=lambda r: r['phase1'])\n    for r in rejections[:20]:\n Compute the store's own median normalized ratio as a size factor.\n    4. Deviation = normalized / size_factor.\n    5. Look for windows matching the recovery pattern shape.\n\n    Returns:\n        rejections: list of (store, product, rejection_day)\n            where rejection_day is the last \"normal\" day before the drop.\n    \"\"\"\n    # Cross-store average demand per (day, product) = calendar signal\n    cross_avg = defaultdict(float)\n    cross_cnt = defaultdict(int)\n    for (day, store, prod), d in agg_demand.items():\n        cross_avg[(day, prod)] += d\n        cross_cnt[(day, prod)] += 1\n    for k in cross_avg:\n        cross_avg[k] /= cross_cnt[k]\n\n    # Per (store, product), normalized trajectory\n    sp_norm = defaultdict(dict)\n    for (day, store, prod), d in agg_demand.items():\n        avg = cross_avg.get((day, prod), 0)\n        if avg > 5:\n            sp_norm[(store, prod)][day] = d / avg\n\n    rejections = []\n\n    for (store, prod), day_norm in sp_norm.items():\n        days_sorted = sorted(day_norm.keys())\n        if len(days_sorted) < 30:\n            continue\n\n        vals = [day_norm[d] for d in days_sorted]\n        # Store size factor: robust estimate of its relative size\n        size_factor = statistics.median(vals)\n        if size_factor < 0.05:\n            continue\n\n        # Day-indexed dict\n        dn = day_norm\n\n        for i, day in enumerate(days_sorted):\n            # Need at least 15 days ahead\n            if day > max(all_days) - 15:\n                continue\n\n            # Current deviation (normalized ratio / size_factor)\n            curr = dn.get(day, size_factor) / size_factor\n\n            # Look at next 14 days\n            future_devs = []\n            for offset in range(1, 15):\n                fd = day + offset\n                future_devs.append(dn.get(fd, size_factor) / size_factor)\n\n            if len(future_devs) < 14:\n                continue\n\n            # Previous 7 days (excluding current)\n            prev_devs = [dn.get(day - j, size_factor) / size_factor\n                         for j in range(1, 8) if (day - j) in dn]\n            if len(prev_devs) < 3:\n                continue\n            prev_avg = statistics.mean(prev_devs)\n\n            # Skip if recent history is already depressed (ongoing recovery)\n            if prev_avg < 0.75:\n                continue\n\n            # Current day should still be near normal\n            if curr < 0.70:\n                continue\n\n            # future_devs[0..2]  = recovery days 1-3  (should be ~20%)\n            # future_devs[3..6]  = recovery days 4-7  (should be ~50%)\n            # future_devs[7..13] = recovery days 8-14 (should be ~80%)\n            phase1 = statistics.mean(future_devs[0:3])\n            phase2 = statistics.mean(future_devs[3:7])\n            phase3 = statistics.mean(future_devs[7:14])\n\n            # Conditions for quality rejection pattern:\n            # phase1 significantly below normal\n            # phase2 > phase1\n            # phase3 > phase2\n            # All phases below the pre-rejection level\n            if (phase1 < 0.55 and\n                phase2 > phase1 * 1.2 and\n                phase3 > phase2 * 1.1 and\n                phase3 < 0.98 and\n                phase2 < 0.85):\n                rejections.append({\n                    'store': store,\n                    'product': prod,\n                    'rejection_day': day,\n                    'phase1': phase1,\n                    'phase2': phase2,\n                    'phase3': phase3,\n                    'prev_avg': prev_avg,\n                })\n\n    return rejections\n\n\n# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n# 5. ATTRIBUTE TO SUPPLIERS\n# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\ndef attribute_rejections(rejections, consumed_by, store_received):\n    \"\"\"\n    For each detected rejection, find the responsible supplier.\n\n    The rejection affects consumers who bought from the bad batch\n    on or just before the rejection_day. So we check which supplier's\n    units were being consumed on rejection_day and the few days before.\n\n    For \"confirmed\" status, we need clear attribution:\n    - The supplier was the sole or dominant source for the store at that time.\n    \"\"\"\n    confirmed = defaultdict(set)\n\n    for rej in rejections:\n        store = rej['store']\n        prod = rej['product']\n        rday = rej['rejection_day']\n\n        # The bad batch was consumed around rday.\n        # Check consumed_by for rday and a window before (batch might span days).\n        candidate_suppliers = defaultdict(int)\n        for check_day in range(max(1, rday - 5), rday + 2):\n            consumed = consumed_by.get((check_day, store, prod), {})\n            for supp, qty in consumed.items():\n                candidate_suppliers[supp] += qty\n\n        if not candidate_suppliers:\n            continue\n\n        total_qty = sum(candidate_suppliers.values())\n        if total_qty == 0:\n            continue\n\n        # Find dominant supplier(s)\n        max_qty = max(candidate_suppliers.values())\n        dominant = [s for s, q in candidate_suppliers.items()\n                    if q >= 0.6 * max_qty and q / total_qty > 0.3]\n\n        # For \"confirmed\" – require strong dominance:\n        # Either sole supplier, or one supplier with >70% of consumed units\n        sole = [s for s, q in candidate_suppliers.items()\n                if q / total_qty > 0.70]\n\n        if sole:\n            for s in sole:\n                confirmed[prod].add(s)\n        elif len(candidate_suppliers) == 1:\n            s = list(candidate_suppliers.keys())[0]\n            confirmed[prod].add(s)\n\n    return confirmed\n\n\n# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n# MAIN\n# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\ndef main():\n    print(\"Step 1: Parsing supplier receipts...\")\n    sup_deliveries = parse_supplier_receipts()\n    print(f\"  {len(sup_deliveries)} days, {sum(len(v) for v in sup_deliveries.values())} records\")\n\n    print(\"Step 2: Parsing wholesaler receipts...\")\n    sup_seq = parse_wholesaler_receipts()\n\n    print(\"Step 3: Parsing store orders...\")\n    store_orders = parse_store_orders()\n\n    print(\"Step 4: Parsing store sequences...\")\n    store_seq = parse_store_seq()\n\n    print(\"Step 5: Parsing sales log...\")\n    agg_demand, agg_sold = parse_sales_log()\n    print(f\"  {len(agg_demand)} (day, store, product) records\")\n\n    all_days = sorted(set(d for d, _, _ in agg_demand.keys()))\n    all_stores = sorted(set(s for _, s, _ in agg_demand.keys()))\n    all_products = sorted(set(p for _, _, p in agg_demand.keys()),\n                          key=lambda x: int(x.split('_')[1]))\n    print(f\"  Days: {min(all_days)}-{max(all_days)}, Stores: {len(all_stores)}, Products: {len(all_products)}\")\n\n    print(\"Step 6: Reconstructing supply chain...\")\n    store_received = reconstruct_supply_chain(sup_deliveries, sup_seq, store_orders, store_seq)\n    print(f\"  {len(store_received)} (day, store, product) allocation records\")\n\n    print(\"Step 7: Building store FIFO inventory...\")\n    consumed_by = build_store_inventory_and_track(\n        store_received, agg_sold, all_days, all_stores, all_products\n    )\n    print(f\"  {len(consumed_by)} consumption records\")\n\n    print(\"Step 8: Detecting quality rejections...\")\n    rejections = detect_quality_rejections(agg_demand, all_days, all_stores, all_products)\n    print(f\"  {len(rejections)} potential quality rejection events found\")\n\n    # Print top rejections for debugging\n    rejections.sort(key=lambda r: r['phase1'])\n    for r in rejections[:20]:\n        print(f\"    {r['store']}, {r['product']}, day={r['rejection_day']}: \"\n              f\"ph1={r['phase1']:.3f}, ph2={r['phase2']:.3f}, ph3={r['phase3']:.3f}\")\n\n    print(\"Step 9: Attributing rejections to suppliers...\")\n    confirmed = attribute_rejections(rejections, consumed_by, store_received)\n\n    # Build final result\n    result = {}\n    for prod in all_products:\n        offenders = sorted(confirmed.get(prod, set()),\n                           key=lambda x: int(x.split('_')[1]))\n        result[prod] = offenders\n\n    print(\"\\n=== CONFIRMED QUALITY OFFENDERS ===\")\n    for prod, offs in result.items():\n        if offs:\n            print(f\"  {prod}: {offs}\")\n\n    # Save\n    with open('/app/answer.json', 'w') as f:\n        json.dump(result, f,
